[9/2/23, 10:09:57â€¯AM] Peter Potts: I thoroughly enjoyed my time at Reed's School. I had a great rapport with the teachers and had a genuine interest in sports, although I had to bid farewell to rugby due to a string of injuries. Looking back, I realize how fortunate we were because California's private schools have relatively modest sports facilities. This led me to transfer my daughter to a public high school, which have impressive setups, although she still showed no interest in sports, which was a bit disappointing.

I scraped admission into Reed's School because of my exceptional math skills only. During that time, my father faced a life-threatening brain tumor with only a 25% chance of survival. We chose Reed's because they promised to keep me enrolled even if the worst happened. Fortunately, my father survived, albeit with some disabilities, and he is now 89 years old.

Over the years, I steadily climbed the academic ranks, eventually becoming a favorite among the teachers during my A-levels. Such was their trust in me that even when I consumed a third of a bottle of whiskey and had an unfortunate encounter with Hewitt's feet, I escaped any punishment. I think they considered the horrendous hangover the following day punishment enough.

I cherish memories of fireworks being launched from our dormitory windows and the time someone mischievously set one off inside the dormitory, causing it to zip around without causing any harm or starting a fire.

My performance at A-levels was outstanding, earning me a place at Cambridge to study Mathematics. However, there was a condition attached â€“ I had to pass an O-level in a foreign language. As a result, I extended my stay at Reed's for an additional year to study Latin; there was no way I was revisiting French.

During that extra year, I received a somewhat regal treatment, complete with my own room in Blathwayt. I even rigged up a sound system that would automatically turn off when the door opened. Poor Hewitt had a run-in with it when he attempted to reprimand me for playing music too loudly.

Upon arriving at Cambridge, I quickly realized I was lagging behind in Mathematics compared to my peers. While everyone else had studied Further Mathematics at A-level, Reed's had never offered that option. In my very first lecture at Cambridge, the professor urged us to forget everything we had learned in school because the real mathematical journey was commencing.

My time at Cambridge was a true eye-opener, offering a challenging and transformative experience. On the sports front, the hockey skills I acquired at Reed's proved incredibly valuable. I earned a spot in the St John's College first team for three years and even had the opportunity to play in the University 3rd team on one occasion.

[9/17/23, 8:10:51â€¯AM] Tom Hardiment: â€This message was deleted.
[9/17/23, 8:28:45â€¯AM] Tom Hardiment: Well remembered Finchie.
When he left Mr Williams replaced him. I did A level art with him. He was a useless teacher and a lazy fecker. He kept bunking off from teaching us to see his girlfriend in London. He asked us to cover for him each time but after a couple of terms we just said to Prince, when he put his head into the art studio, that he was in London.  He was sacked the next week.
His idea of teaching art was to say cut out a picture you like from a magazine, draw a grid over it scale it up and copy it.
Peter Thomas was a friend of Mr Prince and stood in for the last two terms and saved us all from certain failure.
Taught us to sculpt, screen print, throw pots; paint with oil, gouache and water colour and draw with conte, pastel and charcoal. Still life, life classes and from nature.
Without the A for art A Level I wouldn't have got to uni. Whoever employed Mr Williams should've been sacked too.

Still in touch with Peter. He lives in the Dordogne and exhibits in London each year. Lovely guy.

In the studio we (Rob Lee, James G, Joe Moreton and Joe Chan, & Mrs Martin!) listened to Fleetwood Mac - Rumours, Rickie Lee Jones and Van Morrison - Astral Weeks, drank a lot of tea and dyed our hair with peroxide. Good times.
